Debit card numbers are usually 16-digit numbers, consisting of a 6-digit bank identification number (BIN), a 6-digit account number, and a 4-digit card verification value (CVV) or card verification code (CVC).

In the United States, debit card numbers are typically issued by banks and financial institutions to their customers. The first six digits of the card number, the BIN, identify the bank that issued the card. The next six digits are the account number, which is unique to each customer. The final four digits, the CVV or CVC, are used for security purposes to verify the cardholder's identity when making transactions.
